🏗️ Build Commands

Docker build commands enable you to create container images for your anihpj Django project. These commands compile your Django application, install dependencies, configure the environment, and package everything into portable container images that can run consistently across development, staging, and production environments.

📋 Build Commands Overview

docker build - Build images from Dockerfile
docker builder - Manage build cache and builders
docker buildx - Extended build capabilities
docker buildx bake - Build multiple images
docker buildx create - Create builder instances
docker buildx imagetools - Manage multi-arch images
🎯 Django Focus: This documentation shows practical examples of building containerized Django applications using the anihpj project with its jobpost app models (Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost). Learn how to create optimized Docker images, manage build contexts, and implement multi-stage builds for Django production deployments.

docker build

Official Docs: docker build | Docker CLI: docker build

Build Docker images from a Dockerfile and a "context" - a set of files at a specified location.

Full Description

The docker build command constructs Docker images by reading instructions from a Dockerfile. For your anihpj Django project, this command processes your Dockerfile to create container images that include your Django application code, Python dependencies from requirements.txt, static files, database migrations, and all necessary runtime configurations. The build process creates layered images where each Dockerfile instruction creates a new layer, enabling efficient caching and faster subsequent builds.

When building your anihpj Django application, Docker build reads the build context (typically your project directory), copies relevant files into the container, installs Python packages, configures Django settings, runs collectstatic for production deployments, and creates the final image. The resulting image can be used to run containers that serve your jobpost app APIs, handle user authentication, manage author profiles, process location-based queries, and execute JobPost operations.

Syntax

# Basic build from current directory
docker build .

# Build with custom tag
docker build -t {image-name}:{tag} .

# Build with Dockerfile in different location
docker build -f {dockerfile-path} {context-path}

# Build with build arguments
docker build --build-arg {ARG_NAME}={value} -t {image-name} .

# Build with target stage (multi-stage builds)
docker build --target {stage-name} -t {image-name} .

# Build with custom platform
docker build --platform {platform} -t {image-name} .

# Build with progress output
docker build --progress=plain -t {image-name} .

# Build without cache
docker build --no-cache -t {image-name} .

# Build with cache from another image
docker build --cache-from {image-name} -t {new-image} .

Parameters Description

  • context-path: The build context path (usually current directory .). Contains Dockerfile, source code, and files needed for the build. For Django projects, this includes manage.py, apps, requirements.txt, static files, and templates.
  • -t, --tag: Name and optionally tag for the image in format name:tag. Use descriptive tags like anihpj/jobpost-app:v1.0.0 or anihpj/django-dev:latest for different environments and versions.
  • -f, --file: Path to the Dockerfile (default is {context}/Dockerfile). Useful when you have multiple Dockerfiles like Dockerfile.dev, Dockerfile.prod, or Dockerfile.test for different Django deployment scenarios.
  • --build-arg: Set build-time variables that can be used in Dockerfile with ARG instruction. Common Django args include DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE, DEBUG, SECRET_KEY, DATABASE_URL for environment-specific builds.
  • --target: Set target build stage for multi-stage builds. Useful for Django apps with separate development, testing, and production stages in a single Dockerfile.
  • --platform: Set platform if server is multi-platform capable. Specify platforms like linux/amd64, linux/arm64 for Django deployments across different architectures.
  • --progress: Set type of progress output (auto, plain, tty). Use 'plain' for CI/CD pipelines building Django images to get detailed build logs.
  • --no-cache: Do not use cache when building the image. Forces complete rebuild of Django application, useful when you want to ensure latest dependencies or clean build environment.
  • --cache-from: Images to consider as cache sources. Speeds up Django image builds by reusing layers from previous builds or base images.
  • --pull: Always attempt to pull newer version of base image. Ensures your Django image uses latest security updates from base Python images.
  • --quiet, -q: Suppress build output and print image ID on success. Useful for automated Django deployment scripts.
  • --rm: Remove intermediate containers after successful build (default true). Keeps Docker environment clean during Django image builds.
  • --force-rm: Always remove intermediate containers even if build fails. Prevents accumulation of failed Django build containers.

Attributes

  • Image ID: Unique identifier for the built image (SHA256 hash). Used to reference the specific Django image version.
  • Build Context Size: Size of files sent to Docker daemon. Monitor this for Django projects to optimize build performance.
  • Total Build Time: Time taken for complete build process. Track this metric for Django application build optimization.
  • Layer Count: Number of layers in the final image. Each Dockerfile instruction creates a layer affecting Django image size and startup time.
  • Cache Status: Indicates which layers were cached vs rebuilt. Helps optimize Django build times through effective layer caching.

Methods

Build with Build Arguments

Syntax: docker build --build-arg {ARG}={VALUE} -t {image} {context}

Parameters: ARG (string) - Build argument name defined in Dockerfile with ARG instruction, VALUE (string) - Value to pass for the argument

Pass build-time variables to customize Django application builds for different environments, database configurations, or feature flags.

Multi-stage Build Target

Syntax: docker build --target {stage} -t {image} {context}

Parameters: stage (string) - Name of the build stage from Dockerfile FROM instruction with AS alias

Build specific stages of multi-stage Dockerfiles, useful for creating separate Django development, testing, and production images from single Dockerfile.

Cross-platform Build

Syntax: docker build --platform {platform} -t {image} {context}

Parameters: platform (string) - Target platform in format os/architecture like linux/amd64, linux/arm64

Build Django images for specific platforms, essential for deploying to different cloud providers or ARM-based servers.

Return Value

Returns the image ID of successfully built Docker image. On failure, returns non-zero exit code with error details. Build output includes layer information, cache status, and final image summary.

  • Success (0): Image built successfully, returns image ID
  • Error (1): Build failed due to Dockerfile syntax errors, missing files, or build context issues
  • Error (125): Docker daemon error or invalid command usage

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Basic Django Application Build (Skills Model API)

Build a basic Django container image for the Skills model API service with production optimizations and proper layer caching.

Docker Context Setup:

# Create Dockerfile for Skills API service
cat > Dockerfile.skills << 'EOF'
FROM python:3.11-slim

# Set working directory
WORKDIR /app

# Install system dependencies for Django and PostgreSQL
RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y \
    build-essential \
    libpq-dev \
    && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*

# Copy requirements first for better caching
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

# Copy Django project files
COPY . .

# Set Django environment variables
ENV DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE=anihpj.settings
ENV PYTHONPATH=/app
ENV DJANGO_APP=jobpost

# Run Django setup commands
RUN python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

# Expose port for Skills API
EXPOSE 8000

# Start Skills API server
CMD ["python", "manage.py", "runserver", "0.0.0.0:8000"]
EOF
# Build Skills API image with proper tagging
docker build -f Dockerfile.skills -t anihpj/skills-api:v1.0.0 .

Test the built image:

# Run container to test Skills API functionality
docker run -d -p 8000:8000 --name skills-api-test anihpj/skills-api:v1.0.0

# Test Skills model API endpoints
curl http://localhost:8000/jobpost/skills/

Django Model Query Output:

# Execute in Django shell within container
docker exec -it skills-api-test python manage.py shell

# Skills model operations
from jobpost.models import Skills, User, Author, Location, JobPost

# Query Skills objects
skills_queryset = Skills.objects.all()
print("Skills QuerySet:", skills_queryset)
print("Skills Count:", skills_queryset.count())

# Show Skills objects with details
for skill in skills_queryset:
    print(f"Skill: {skill.name} - {skill.description} ({skill.level})")
Skills QuerySet: , , , , ]> Skills Count: 5 Skill: Python - Python programming language (Advanced) Skill: Django - Django web framework (Expert) Skill: PostgreSQL - PostgreSQL database management (Intermediate) Skill: Docker - Container platform (Intermediate) Skill: Kubernetes - Container orchestration (Beginner)
Example 2: Multi-stage Build for User Authentication Service

Create a multi-stage Docker build that separates development dependencies from production deployment for the User authentication service, optimizing final image size.

Multi-stage Dockerfile Setup:

# Create multi-stage Dockerfile for User auth service
cat > Dockerfile.user-auth << 'EOF'
# Development stage with all tools
FROM python:3.11 as development
WORKDIR /app
COPY requirements-dev.txt .
RUN pip install -r requirements-dev.txt
COPY . .
RUN python manage.py test

# Production stage with minimal dependencies
FROM python:3.11-slim as production
WORKDIR /app

# Install only runtime system dependencies
RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y \
    libpq-dev \
    && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/* \
    && apt-get clean

# Create non-root user for security
RUN groupadd -r django && useradd -r -g django django

# Copy only production requirements
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

# Copy application code
COPY --chown=django:django . .

# Run Django production setup
RUN python manage.py collectstatic --noinput
RUN python manage.py compilemessages

# Switch to non-root user
USER django

EXPOSE 8001

CMD ["gunicorn", "--bind", "0.0.0.0:8001", "anihpj.wsgi:application"]
EOF
# Build production target for User authentication service
docker build -f Dockerfile.user-auth --target production -t anihpj/user-auth:production .
Sending build context to Docker daemon 52.8MB Step 1/15 : FROM python:3.11 as development ---> 2a3b4c5d6e7f Step 2/15 : WORKDIR /app ---> Using cache ---> 8g7f6e5d4c3b Step 3/15 : COPY requirements-dev.txt . ---> 9h8g7f6e5d4c Step 4/15 : RUN pip install -r requirements-dev.txt ---> Running in 0i9h8g7f6e5d Collecting Django==6.0 Collecting pytest==7.4.2 Collecting coverage==7.3.1 ... ---> 1j0i9h8g7f6e Step 5/15 : COPY . . ---> 2k1j0i9h8g7f Step 6/15 : RUN python manage.py test ---> Running in 3l2k1j0i9h8g System check identified no issues (0 silenced). .................... Ran 20 tests in 2.456s OK ---> 4m3l2k1j0i9h Step 7/15 : FROM python:3.11-slim as production 3.11-slim: Pulling from library/python ... ---> 5n4m3l2k1j0i Step 8/15 : WORKDIR /app ---> Running in 6o5n4m3l2k1j ---> 7p6o5n4m3l2k Step 9/15 : RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y ... ---> Running in 8q7p6o5n4m3l ---> 9r8q7p6o5n4m Step 10/15 : RUN groupadd -r django && useradd -r -g django django ---> Running in 0s9r8q7p6o5n ---> 1t0s9r8q7p6o Step 11/15 : COPY requirements.txt . ---> 2u1t0s9r8q7p Step 12/15 : RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt ---> Running in 3v2u1t0s9r8q ---> 4w3v2u1t0s9r Step 13/15 : COPY --chown=django:django . . ---> 5x4w3v2u1t0s Step 14/15 : RUN python manage.py collectstatic --noinput ---> Running in 6y5x4w3v2u1t 128 static files copied to '/app/static'. ---> 7z6y5x4w3v2u Step 15/15 : USER django ---> Running in 8a7z6y5x4w3v ---> 9b8a7z6y5x4w Successfully built 9b8a7z6y5x4w Successfully tagged anihpj/user-auth:production

Test User authentication functionality:

# Run User authentication service
docker run -d -p 8001:8001 --name user-auth-prod anihpj/user-auth:production

# Test User authentication endpoints
curl -X POST http://localhost:8001/api/auth/login/ \
     -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
     -d '{"username": "testuser", "password": "testpass123"}'
{ "access_token": "eyJ0eXAiOiJKV1QiLCJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9...", "refresh_token": "eyJ0eXAiOiJKV1QiLCJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9...", "user": { "id": 1, "username": "testuser", "email": "test@example.com", "first_name": "Test", "last_name": "User", "date_joined": "2026-01-11T10:35:00Z" } }

User Model Query Operations:

# Execute User model queries in container
docker exec -it user-auth-prod python manage.py shell

# User and Author model operations  
from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author, Skills, Location, JobPost

# Query User objects with related Author profiles
users_with_authors = User.objects.select_related('author').all()
print("Users with Authors:", users_with_authors)

# Create relationships between models
for user in users_with_authors[:3]:
    print(f"User: {user.username} - Author: {getattr(user, 'author', None)}")

Parameterized Dockerfile:

# Create Dockerfile with build arguments for Author service

FROM python:3.11-slim

# Define build arguments with defaults
ARG DJANGO_ENV=production
ARG DEBUG=False
ARG MEDIA_ROOT=/app/media
ARG ALLOWED_HOSTS=localhost
ARG DATABASE_URL=postgresql://localhost/anihpj

    libpq-dev \
    $(if [ "$DJANGO_ENV" = "development" ]; then echo "vim curl"; fi) \
    && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*

# Copy and install Python dependencies
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

# Install dev dependencies in development environment

        pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements-dev.txt; \
    fi

# Copy application code
COPY . .

# Set environment variables from build args

ENV DEBUG=$DEBUG
ENV MEDIA_ROOT=$MEDIA_ROOT
ENV ALLOWED_HOSTS=$ALLOWED_HOSTS
ENV DATABASE_URL=$DATABASE_URL

# Create media directory for Author uploads

EXPOSE 8002

# Use different commands based on environment

        python manage.py runserver 0.0.0.0:8002; \
    else \
        gunicorn --bind 0.0.0.0:8002 anihpj.wsgi:application; \
    fi
EOF

    --build-arg DJANGO_ENV=development \
    --build-arg DEBUG=True \

    -t anihpj/author-service:dev .

Example 4: Cross-platform Build for Location Service

Build Location service Docker image for multiple architectures (AMD64 and ARM64) to support deployment across different cloud providers and development environments.

Platform-aware Dockerfile:

# Create Dockerfile with platform-specific optimizations
cat > Dockerfile.location << 'EOF'
FROM python:3.11-slim

# Use build platform for architecture-specific optimizations
ARG TARGETPLATFORM
ARG BUILDPLATFORM

WORKDIR /app

# Install platform-specific dependencies
RUN echo "Building for $TARGETPLATFORM on $BUILDPLATFORM" && \
    apt-get update && apt-get install -y \
    libpq-dev \
    $(if [ "$TARGETPLATFORM" = "linux/arm64" ]; then echo "gcc-aarch64-linux-gnu"; fi) \
    && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*

# Copy requirements and install Python packages
COPY requirements-geo.txt .
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements-geo.txt

# Install platform-specific geo libraries
RUN if [ "$TARGETPLATFORM" = "linux/amd64" ]; then \
        pip install --no-cache-dir geopy[speedups]; \
    else \
        pip install --no-cache-dir geopy; \
    fi

# Copy application code
COPY . .

# Set environment for Location service
ENV DJANGO_APP=location
ENV GEO_SERVICE=enabled
ENV CACHE_BACKEND=redis

# Setup static files and geo data
RUN python manage.py collectstatic --noinput
RUN python manage.py setup_geo_data

EXPOSE 8003

CMD ["gunicorn", "--bind", "0.0.0.0:8003", "--workers", "4", "anihpj.wsgi:application"]
EOF
# Build Location service for multiple platforms
docker build -f Dockerfile.location --platform linux/amd64 -t anihpj/location-service:amd64 .
docker build -f Dockerfile.location --platform linux/arm64 -t anihpj/location-service:arm64 .

# Test Location model geographic capabilities

from jobpost.models import Location, JobPost, Author, Skills, User
from django.contrib.gis.measure import Distance
from django.contrib.gis.geos import Point

# Query locations near coordinates
sf_point = Point(-122.4194, 37.7749, srid=4326)
nearby_locations = Location.objects.filter(
    point__distance_lte=(sf_point, Distance(mi=50))
)
print("Nearby Locations:", nearby_locations)

# Query JobPosts by location
for location in nearby_locations:
    job_count = JobPost.objects.filter(location=location).count()
    print(f"Location: {location.name} - Jobs: {job_count}")

Example 5: Optimized Build with Cache Layers (JobPost Processing Service)

Build JobPost processing service with advanced caching strategies, layer optimization, and build context minimization for fast iterative development and CI/CD pipelines.

Optimized Dockerfile with cache layers:

# Create .dockerignore for optimal build context
cat > .dockerignore << 'EOF'
.git
.gitignore
README.md
.pytest_cache
.coverage
*.pyc
__pycache__
.venv
node_modules
.env.local
.env.development
.env.test
media/temp
logs/*.log
EOF

# Create optimized Dockerfile for JobPost service
cat > Dockerfile.jobpost << 'EOF'
FROM python:3.11-slim as base

# Create app user for security
RUN groupadd -r jobpost && useradd -r -g jobpost jobpost

# Install system dependencies (cached layer)
RUN apt-get update && apt-get install -y \
    libpq-dev \
    && rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/* \
    && apt-get clean

FROM base as dependencies

WORKDIR /app

# Copy only requirements files for caching
COPY requirements.txt requirements-celery.txt ./

# Install Python dependencies (cached layer)
RUN pip install --no-cache-dir --upgrade pip && \
    pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt && \
    pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements-celery.txt

FROM dependencies as application

# Copy application code (frequently changing layer)
COPY --chown=jobpost:jobpost . .

# Django setup commands
RUN python manage.py collectstatic --noinput
RUN python manage.py check --deploy

# Create necessary directories
RUN mkdir -p /app/logs /app/media/jobpost && \
    chown -R jobpost:jobpost /app/logs /app/media

USER jobpost

EXPOSE 8004

# Health check
HEALTHCHECK --interval=30s --timeout=10s --start-period=5s --retries=3 \
    CMD curl -f http://localhost:8004/health/ || exit 1

CMD ["celery", "worker", "-A", "anihpj", "--loglevel=info"]
EOF
# Build with cache optimization and progress output
docker build -f Dockerfile.jobpost \
    --cache-from anihpj/jobpost-base:latest \
    --progress=plain \
    -t anihpj/jobpost-processor:v2.0.0 .

JobPost Model Complex Queries:

# Execute complex JobPost queries in container
docker exec -it jobpost-processor python manage.py shell

from jobpost.models import JobPost, Author, Skills, Location, User
from django.db.models import Count, Q, Prefetch

# Complex JobPost queries with relationships
complex_queryset = JobPost.objects.select_related('author', 'location').prefetch_related(
    Prefetch('skills', queryset=Skills.objects.filter(level__in=['Advanced', 'Expert']))
).filter(
    Q(location__name__icontains='San Francisco') | Q(remote_friendly=True)
).annotate(
    skills_count=Count('skills')
).order_by('-created_at')

print("Complex JobPost QuerySet:", complex_queryset)

# Analyze JobPost distribution
for job in complex_queryset[:3]:
    print(f"Job: {job.title}")
    print(f"  Author: {job.author.username}")
    print(f"  Location: {job.location.name}")
    print(f"  Skills: {[s.name for s in job.skills.all()]}")
    print(f"  Skills Count: {job.skills_count}")
    print("---")

docker builder

Official Docs: docker builder | Docker CLI: docker builder

Manage the builder environment for Docker builds, including cache management and builder instance configuration.

Full Description

The docker builder command manages Docker build environments, providing advanced build cache management and builder instance configuration. For your anihpj Django project, this command helps optimize build performance by managing build cache, configuring build environments, and cleaning up unnecessary build artifacts. The builder system enables faster iterative development by reusing cached layers from previous Django application builds.

Builder management is crucial for Django development workflows where you frequently rebuild images during development cycles. Proper cache management ensures that your jobpost app builds leverage cached layers for unchanged dependencies, static files, and Django setup commands, significantly reducing build times for Skills, User, Author, Location, and JobPost service containers.

Syntax

# Show builder disk usage
docker builder prune

# Remove build cache (interactive)
docker builder prune

# Remove all unused build cache without prompt
docker builder prune -f

# Remove build cache with specific filters
docker builder prune --filter until=24h

# Show builder storage usage
docker system df

# Remove build cache older than specified time
docker builder prune --filter until=72h --force

Parameters Description

  • prune: Remove unused build cache to free up disk space. Essential for Django development environments where frequent builds can accumulate significant cache data from dependency installations, static file collection, and application layer builds.
  • -f, --force: Do not prompt for confirmation before removing cache. Useful in automated Django CI/CD pipelines where interactive prompts would halt the build process.
  • --filter: Provide filter values to selectively remove cache entries. Common filters include 'until' for time-based cleanup, 'label' for labeled cache entries, and 'type' for specific cache types in Django build workflows.
  • --all, -a: Remove all unused cache, not just dangling cache. More aggressive cleanup that removes all build cache including partially used cache from Django application layers.
  • --keep-storage: Amount of disk space to keep for cache. Specify in bytes, KB, MB, or GB to maintain optimal cache size for Django project builds without exhausting disk space.

Attributes

  • Cache Size: Total disk space consumed by build cache. Monitor this to optimize Django build performance while managing storage resources.
  • Reclaimable Space: Amount of space that can be freed by pruning unused cache. Important metric for maintaining efficient Django development environments.
  • Cache Entries: Number of cached build layers stored. Each Django build instruction creates cache entries that can be reused in subsequent builds.
  • Last Used: Timestamp when cache entries were last accessed. Helps identify stale cache from Django builds that can be safely removed.

Methods

Prune with Time Filter

Syntax: docker builder prune --filter until={time}

Parameters: time (duration) - Time duration like 24h, 7d, 1w for removing cache older than specified time

Remove Django build cache older than specified duration to maintain recent cache while freeing space from outdated dependency and application builds.

Forced Cache Cleanup

Syntax: docker builder prune --all --force

Parameters: --all (boolean) - Remove all cache including active cache, --force (boolean) - Skip confirmation prompt

Aggressively clean all build cache without prompts, useful for Django development environment reset or CI/CD pipeline cleanup stages.

Return Value

Returns information about cache cleanup operations including total space reclaimed, number of cache entries removed, and remaining cache statistics. Success operations return zero exit code, while errors return non-zero codes with descriptive messages.

  • Success (0): Cache cleanup completed successfully
  • Error (1): General error in cache operations
  • Error (125): Docker daemon error or invalid command usage

Example 2: Automated Cache Cleanup for User Authentication Service

Implement automated build cache management for User authentication service in CI/CD pipeline with time-based cleanup strategies.

# Create automated cleanup script for User auth service
cat > cleanup-user-auth-cache.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash
echo "=== User Auth Service Cache Cleanup ==="

# Show current cache status
echo "Current build cache usage:"
docker system df --format "table {{.Type}}\t{{.TotalCount}}\t{{.Size}}\t{{.Reclaimable}}"

# Clean cache older than 48 hours (development cycle)
echo "Cleaning cache older than 48 hours..."
docker builder prune --filter until=48h --force

# Clean all cache if usage exceeds 2GB
CACHE_SIZE=$(docker system df --format "{{.Size}}" | grep "Build Cache" | cut -d' ' -f1)
if [[ "$CACHE_SIZE" > "2GB" ]]; then
    echo "Cache size ($CACHE_SIZE) exceeds limit, performing full cleanup..."
    docker builder prune --all --force
fi

echo "Cache cleanup completed"
EOF

chmod +x cleanup-user-auth-cache.sh
# Execute automated cache cleanup
./cleanup-user-auth-cache.sh

# Test User model operations after cache cleanup

from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author, Skills, Location, JobPost
from django.core.cache import cache

# User model performance after cache reset
users = User.objects.select_related().all()
print("Users after cache cleanup:", users.count())

# Cache warming for User-related queries
for user in users:
    if hasattr(user, 'author'):
        cache.set(f'user_profile_{user.id}', user.author, 3600)
        
print("Cache status after warming:", cache.get('user_profile_1') is not None)

Example 3: Selective Cache Management for Author Content Service

Implement selective build cache management for Author content service using labels and filters to preserve critical cache while cleaning development artifacts.

# Create labeled Dockerfile for Author service cache management
cat > Dockerfile.author-labeled << 'EOF'
FROM python:3.11-slim

# Add cache labels for selective cleanup
LABEL cache.type="author-service"
LABEL cache.env="development" 
LABEL cache.version="v2.1"

WORKDIR /app

# Labeled requirements layer for cache retention
COPY requirements.txt .
RUN --mount=type=cache,target=/root/.cache/pip,sharing=shared \
    pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt

# Copy application with cache labels
COPY . .

# Author service specific setup with cache labels
RUN --mount=type=cache,target=/tmp/author-cache \
    python manage.py collectstatic --noinput && \
    python manage.py setup_author_data

EXPOSE 8002
CMD ["gunicorn", "--bind", "0.0.0.0:8002", "anihpj.wsgi:application"]
EOF

DOCKER_BUILDKIT=1 docker build -f Dockerfile.author-labeled -t anihpj/author-service:labeled .

Example 5: Advanced Cache Analytics for JobPost Processing

Implement comprehensive cache analytics and monitoring for JobPost processing service to optimize build performance and resource utilization across development lifecycle.

# Create cache analytics script for JobPost service
cat > analyze-jobpost-cache.sh << 'EOF'
#!/bin/bash
echo "=== JobPost Service Cache Analytics ==="

# Get detailed cache statistics
echo "Detailed Cache Analysis:"
docker system df --format "{{.Type}}: {{.TotalCount}} items, {{.Size}} total, {{.Reclaimable}} reclaimable"

# Show cache age distribution
echo -e "\nCache Age Analysis:"
docker builder prune --filter until=1h --dry-run 2>/dev/null | grep "Total:" || echo "No cache older than 1h"
docker builder prune --filter until=24h --dry-run 2>/dev/null | grep "Total:" || echo "No cache older than 24h"
docker builder prune --filter until=7d --dry-run 2>/dev/null | grep "Total:" || echo "No cache older than 7d"

# Cache efficiency metrics
echo -e "\nCache Efficiency Metrics:"
TOTAL_CACHE=$(docker system df --format "{{.Size}}" | grep -E "Build Cache" | head -1)
RECLAIMABLE=$(docker system df --format "{{.Reclaimable}}" | grep -E "Build Cache" | head -1)
echo "Total Cache: $TOTAL_CACHE"
echo "Reclaimable: $RECLAIMABLE"
echo "Cache Efficiency: $(echo "$TOTAL_CACHE $RECLAIMABLE" | awk '{if($1 > 0) print 100-(($2/$1)*100) "% active"}' || echo "N/A")"
EOF

chmod +x analyze-jobpost-cache.sh
# Run comprehensive cache analysis
./analyze-jobpost-cache.sh

JobPost Model Cache-Optimized Analytics:

# Comprehensive JobPost model analysis with cache optimization
docker exec -it jobpost-analytics python manage.py shell

from jobpost.models import JobPost, Author, Skills, Location, User
from django.db.models import Count, Q, Avg, Max
from django.core.cache import cache
import time

# Cache-aware complex JobPost analytics
start_time = time.time()
jobpost_analytics = JobPost.objects.select_related('author', 'location').prefetch_related('skills').aggregate(
    total_posts=Count('id'),
    avg_skills_per_job=Avg('skills__id'),
    max_salary=Max('salary_max'),
    remote_percentage=Count('id', filter=Q(remote_friendly=True)) * 100.0 / Count('id')
)
query_time = time.time() - start_time

print("JobPost Analytics (Cache-Optimized):")
print(f"Query Time: {query_time:.4f}s")
for key, value in jobpost_analytics.items():
    print(f"{key}: {value}")

# Model relationships analysis
print("\nModel Relationship Summary:")
print(f"Total JobPosts: {JobPost.objects.count()}")
print(f"Total Authors: {Author.objects.count()}")
print(f"Total Skills: {Skills.objects.count()}")
print(f"Total Locations: {Location.objects.count()}")

docker buildx

Official Docs: docker buildx | Docker CLI: docker buildx

Extended build capabilities with support for multi-platform builds, advanced caching, and BuildKit features for modern container workflows.

Full Description

The docker buildx command provides extended build capabilities beyond the standard docker build functionality. For your anihpj Django project, buildx enables multi-platform container builds, advanced caching strategies, concurrent builds, and modern BuildKit features. This is essential when deploying Django applications across different architectures (AMD64, ARM64) or when building for multiple environments simultaneously.

Buildx is particularly valuable for Django development teams that need to build container images for different deployment targets - from local development on Apple Silicon Macs to production deployment on AMD64 cloud infrastructure. The command manages multiple builder instances, supports BuildKit's advanced features like cache mounts and secrets, and enables efficient CI/CD pipelines for your jobpost application across various platforms.

Syntax

# List available builders
docker buildx ls

# Create new builder instance
docker buildx create --name {builder-name} --driver {driver}

# Use specific builder
docker buildx use {builder-name}

# Build for multiple platforms
docker buildx build --platform linux/amd64,linux/arm64 -t {image-name} .

# Build with advanced features
docker buildx build --cache-from type=registry,ref={cache-image} --cache-to type=registry,ref={cache-image} .

# Inspect builder capabilities
docker buildx inspect {builder-name}

# Remove builder instance
docker buildx rm {builder-name}

# Bootstrap builder (ensure it's ready)
docker buildx inspect --bootstrap {builder-name}

Parameters Description

  • --platform: Target platforms for multi-architecture builds in format os/architecture. Specify multiple platforms comma-separated like linux/amd64,linux/arm64 for Django applications that need to run on different infrastructures.
  • --builder: Name of builder instance to use for the build. Different builders can have different configurations, drivers, and capabilities optimized for specific Django deployment scenarios.
  • --driver: Driver for the builder instance (docker, docker-container, kubernetes). Each driver provides different capabilities for Django build workflows and deployment environments.
  • --cache-from: External cache sources to import during build. Supports registry, local, gha (GitHub Actions), s3, and other cache backends to accelerate Django application builds.
  • --cache-to: External cache destinations to export after build. Enables cache sharing between Django development team members and CI/CD systems.
  • --push: Push the built image to registry immediately after successful build. Streamlines Django application deployment by combining build and publish steps.
  • --load: Load build result to local Docker images after build. Useful for testing Django applications locally after multi-platform builds.
  • --output: Output destination and format for build results. Can export to local filesystem, registry, or other formats beyond standard Docker images.

Attributes

  • Builder Name: Unique identifier for builder instances. Each builder can have different configurations for various Django deployment scenarios.
  • Driver Type: Builder driver that determines available features and performance characteristics for Django builds.
  • Platform Support: List of architectures and operating systems supported by the builder for Django multi-platform deployments.
  • Node Endpoints: Network endpoints where builder nodes are available, important for distributed Django build workflows.
  • Builder Status: Current state of builder instance (running, stopped, error) affecting Django build availability.

Methods

Create Multi-Platform Builder

Syntax: docker buildx create --name {name} --driver docker-container --platform {platforms}

Parameters: name (string) - Builder instance name, driver (string) - Builder driver type, platform (string) - Supported platforms

Create builder instances optimized for Django multi-platform builds supporting different deployment architectures.

Build with Registry Cache

Syntax: docker buildx build --cache-from type=registry,ref={ref} --cache-to type=registry,ref={ref}

Parameters: ref (string) - Registry reference for cache storage and retrieval

Enable distributed cache sharing for Django builds across development team and CI/CD systems using registry-based cache.

Concurrent Platform Build

Syntax: docker buildx build --platform {platform1},{platform2} --push -t {image}

Parameters: platform (string) - Comma-separated list of target platforms

Build Django applications for multiple architectures simultaneously and push to registry for cross-platform deployment.

Return Value

Returns build results including image digests, manifest information, and platform-specific details. For multi-platform builds, returns manifest list with references to platform-specific images. Build failures return detailed error information including platform-specific failure details.

  • Success (0): Build completed successfully for all requested platforms
  • Error (1): Build failed on one or more platforms with detailed error messages
  • Error (125): BuildKit daemon error or invalid buildx configuration

Example 2: Registry Cache Build for User Authentication

User Model Cache Performance Analysis:

# Analyze User model performance with registry cache
docker exec -it user-auth-cached python manage.py shell

from django.contrib.auth.models import User
from jobpost.models import Author, Skills, Location, JobPost
from django.core.cache import cache
import time

# User authentication performance with cached build
start = time.time()
users = User.objects.select_related('author').prefetch_related('author__skills')
user_data = [(u.username, getattr(u, 'author', None)) for u in users]
query_time = time.time() - start

print(f"User Query Performance (Cached Build): {query_time:.4f}s")
print(f"Total Users: {len(user_data)}")

for username, author in user_data[:5]:
    author_name = author.username if author else "No Author"
    print(f"User: {username} -> Author: {author_name}")

Example 4: Advanced Location Service with Secret Mounts

Build Location service with BuildKit advanced features including secret mounts for API keys, SSH agent forwarding, and security-enhanced builds for geographic data processing.

# Create secrets for Location service build
echo "geo_api_key=sk_geo_abcd1234" > geo-secrets.txt
echo "maps_token=pk.eyJ1234" >> geo-secrets.txt

# Create Dockerfile with secret mounts
cat > Dockerfile.location-secure << 'EOF'
# syntax=docker/dockerfile:1
FROM python:3.11-slim

WORKDIR /app

# Use secret mount for API keys during build
RUN --mount=type=secret,id=geo-secrets \
    apt-get update && apt-get install -y \
    libpq-dev curl && \
    rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*

# Copy requirements and install with secret access
COPY requirements-geo.txt .
RUN --mount=type=secret,id=geo-secrets \
    pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements-geo.txt && \
    pip install --no-cache-dir geopy requests

# Copy application code
COPY . .

# Setup geo data with secure API access
RUN --mount=type=secret,id=geo-secrets \
    export $(cat /run/secrets/geo-secrets | xargs) && \
    python manage.py setup_geo_apis && \
    python manage.py collectstatic --noinput

EXPOSE 8003
CMD ["gunicorn", "--bind", "0.0.0.0:8003", "anihpj.wsgi:application"]
EOF
# Build Location service with secrets
docker buildx build \
    --secret id=geo-secrets,src=./geo-secrets.txt \
    --platform linux/amd64,linux/arm64 \
    -t anihpj/location-service:secure \
    --push \
    -f Dockerfile.location-secure .

from jobpost.models import Location, JobPost, Author, Skills, User
from django.contrib.gis.geos import Point
from django.contrib.gis.measure import Distance
import os

# Location model with secure API integration
print("Secure Location Service Build")
print(f"API Keys Configured: {bool(os.getenv('GEO_API_CONFIGURED'))}")

# Geographic queries with secure build
sf_point = Point(-122.4194, 37.7749, srid=4326)
nearby_locations = Location.objects.filter(
    point__distance_lte=(sf_point, Distance(mi=30))
).order_by('name')

print("Nearby Locations (Secure Build):")
for location in nearby_locations:
    distance = sf_point.distance(location.point) * 100  # Convert to km
    print(f"  {location.name}: {distance:.1f}km")
    
# Location-based job distribution
location_jobs = {}
for location in nearby_locations:
    job_count = JobPost.objects.filter(location=location).count()
    location_jobs[location.name] = job_count
    
print("Job Distribution:", location_jobs)

Example 5: JobPost Processing with BuildKit Experimental Features

Build JobPost processing service using experimental BuildKit features including inline cache, advanced networking, and performance optimization for high-throughput job processing workflows.

# Enable BuildKit experimental features
export DOCKER_CLI_EXPERIMENTAL=enabled
export DOCKER_BUILDKIT=1

# Create experimental Dockerfile for JobPost processing
cat > Dockerfile.jobpost-experimental << 'EOF'
# syntax=docker/dockerfile:1.6-labs
FROM python:3.11-slim as base

# Use experimental cache inline feature
RUN --mount=type=cache,target=/var/cache/apt,sharing=shared \
    --mount=type=cache,target=/var/lib/apt,sharing=shared \
    apt-get update && apt-get install -y \
    libpq-dev build-essential && \
    rm -rf /var/lib/apt/lists/*

FROM base as dependencies
WORKDIR /app

# Advanced cache mounting for pip
COPY requirements-jobpost.txt requirements-celery.txt ./
RUN --mount=type=cache,target=/root/.cache/pip,sharing=shared \
    --mount=type=cache,target=/tmp/pip-build,sharing=shared \
    pip wheel --wheel-dir /tmp/pip-build -r requirements-jobpost.txt && \
    pip wheel --wheel-dir /tmp/pip-build -r requirements-celery.txt && \
    pip install --no-index --find-links /tmp/pip-build \
    -r requirements-jobpost.txt -r requirements-celery.txt

FROM dependencies as application

# Copy application with experimental features
COPY --exclude=.git --exclude=__pycache__ . .

# Parallel static file processing
RUN --network=none \
    python manage.py collectstatic --noinput --parallel 4 && \
    python manage.py check --deploy

# Create optimized user
RUN groupadd -r jobpost && useradd -r -g jobpost jobpost && \
    chown -R jobpost:jobpost /app
USER jobpost

EXPOSE 8004
HEALTHCHECK --interval=30s --timeout=10s --start-period=5s --retries=3 \
    CMD curl -f http://localhost:8004/health/ || exit 1

CMD ["celery", "worker", "-A", "anihpj", "--loglevel=info", "--concurrency=4"]
EOF
# Build with experimental features and inline cache
docker buildx build \
    --cache-from type=inline \
    --cache-to type=inline \
    --platform linux/amd64,linux/arm64 \
    -t anihpj/jobpost-processor:experimental \
    --push \
    --progress=plain \
    -f Dockerfile.jobpost-experimental .

JobPost Model Experimental Build Performance:

# Test JobPost model with experimental build optimizations

from jobpost.models import JobPost, Author, Skills, Location, User
from django.db.models import Count, Q, Avg, F
from django.core.cache import cache
import time

# Performance test with experimental build
start_time = time.time()

# Complex JobPost analytics with experimental optimizations
experimental_analytics = JobPost.objects.select_related(
    'author', 'location'
).prefetch_related('skills').annotate(
    skills_count=Count('skills'),
    location_jobs=Count('location__jobpost', distinct=True)
).filter(
    Q(remote_friendly=True) | Q(location__name__icontains='San Francisco')
).order_by('-created_at')

# Execute complex queries
results = list(experimental_analytics[:10])
total_time = time.time() - start_time

print(f"Experimental Build Performance: {total_time:.4f}s")
print(f"Jobs Processed: {len(results)}")

print("\nTop JobPosts (Experimental Build):")
for job in results[:5]:
    print(f"  {job.title} - {job.skills_count} skills - {job.location.name}")
    
# Cache performance
cache_key = 'jobpost_analytics_experimental'
cache.set(cache_key, results, 3600)
print(f"Cache Status: {cache.get(cache_key) is not None}")

docker buildx bake

Official Docs: docker buildx bake | Docker CLI: docker buildx bake

Build multiple images concurrently from a single configuration file, enabling complex multi-service Django application deployments with coordinated builds.

Full Description

The docker buildx bake command enables building multiple related container images concurrently from a single configuration file (HCL, JSON, or docker-compose.yml). For your anihpj Django project, bake is essential when you need to build multiple services simultaneously - such as the web application, worker processes, database initialization containers, and auxiliary services like Redis or Nginx.

Bake configurations allow you to define complex build relationships, shared variables, inheritance between targets, and conditional builds based on environment variables. This is particularly powerful for Django microservices architectures where you need to build the main Django app, Celery workers, database migration containers, static file servers, and monitoring services all with consistent tagging, platform support, and build arguments.

Syntax

# Bake all targets from default bake file
docker buildx bake

# Bake specific targets
docker buildx bake {target1} {target2}

# Bake with custom configuration file  
docker buildx bake -f {bake-file.hcl}

# Bake with variable overrides
docker buildx bake --set {target.args.VAR=value}

# Bake with JSON override
docker buildx bake --set {target.platforms=linux/amd64,linux/arm64}

# Print configuration without building
docker buildx bake --print

# Bake from docker-compose file
docker buildx bake -f docker-compose.yml --push

# Bake with progress output
docker buildx bake --progress {auto|plain|tty}

Parameters Description

  • -f, --file: Bake configuration file path (docker-bake.hcl, docker-compose.yml, or JSON). Defines all build targets, dependencies, and shared configurations for Django services.
  • --print: Print the resolved build configuration without executing builds. Useful for validating Django service build definitions and debugging complex configurations.
  • --progress: Set type of progress output during concurrent builds (auto, plain, tty). Important for monitoring multiple Django service builds simultaneously.
  • --push: Push all built images to registry after successful builds. Enables automated deployment workflows for entire Django application stack.
  • --load: Load built images to local Docker daemon. Useful for testing complete Django application stack locally after multi-service builds.
  • --set: Override build configuration values dynamically. Allows runtime customization of Django build arguments, platforms, or outputs without modifying bake files.
  • --no-cache: Build all targets without using cache. Ensures clean builds for Django services when dependency or configuration changes require complete rebuilds.
  • --pull: Always attempt to pull newer versions of base images for all targets. Keeps Django service builds up-to-date with latest security patches.

Attributes

  • Target Names: Identifiers for individual build targets representing different Django services or deployment configurations.
  • Group Definitions: Collections of related targets that can be built together, useful for Django application tiers (frontend, backend, workers).
  • Variable Inheritance: Shared build arguments and configurations across multiple Django service targets.
  • Platform Matrix: Platform specifications that apply across multiple targets for consistent Django cross-platform deployments.
  • Output Destinations: Registry locations, local paths, or other output formats for built Django service images.

Methods

Multi-Service Django Build

Syntax: docker buildx bake -f django-services.hcl --push

Parameters: file (string) - HCL configuration file defining Django service targets

Build all Django application services (web, workers, utilities) concurrently with shared configuration and coordinated deployment.

Environment-Specific Configuration

Syntax: docker buildx bake --set webapp.args.DJANGO_ENV=production --set webapp.platforms=linux/amd64

Parameters: target configuration overrides for Django environment-specific builds

Override Django build configurations for different deployment environments (development, staging, production) without modifying bake files.

Selective Target Building

Syntax: docker buildx bake django-web celery-worker

Parameters: target names to build selectively from Django application stack

Build specific Django services while maintaining shared configurations and dependencies between targets.

Return Value

Returns build results for all targets including individual success/failure status, image digests, and timing information. Failed targets provide detailed error messages while successful targets return registry information and image metadata.

  • Success (0): All specified targets built successfully
  • Error (1): One or more targets failed with individual error details
  • Error (2): Configuration file parsing error or invalid target definitions

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Complete Django Application Stack Bake

Build entire anihpj Django application including web server, Celery workers, Redis cache, and Nginx proxy using a comprehensive bake configuration for production deployment.

Create comprehensive bake configuration:

# docker-bake.anihpj.hcl
variable "REGISTRY" {
  default = "anihpj"
}

variable "VERSION" {
  default = "latest"
}

variable "PLATFORMS" {
  default = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
}

group "django-stack" {
  targets = ["django-web", "celery-worker", "celery-beat", "nginx-proxy"]
}

target "django-base" {
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.base"
  contexts = {
    app = "."
  }
  args = {
    PYTHON_VERSION = "3.11"
    DJANGO_VERSION = "6.0"
  }
}

target "django-web" {
  inherits = ["django-base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.web"
  tags = ["${REGISTRY}/django-web:${VERSION}"]
  platforms = PLATFORMS
  target = "production"
  args = {
    DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE = "anihpj.settings.production"
    STATIC_ROOT = "/app/staticfiles"
  }
}

target "celery-worker" {
  inherits = ["django-base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.celery"
  tags = ["${REGISTRY}/celery-worker:${VERSION}"]
  platforms = PLATFORMS
  args = {
    WORKER_CONCURRENCY = "4"
    CELERY_APP = "anihpj"
  }
}

target "celery-beat" {
  inherits = ["django-base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.celery-beat"
  tags = ["${REGISTRY}/celery-beat:${VERSION}"]
  platforms = PLATFORMS
}

target "nginx-proxy" {
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.nginx"
  tags = ["${REGISTRY}/nginx-proxy:${VERSION}"]
  platforms = PLATFORMS
  contexts = {
    static = "./staticfiles"
    config = "./nginx"
  }
}
# Bake complete Django application stack
docker buildx bake -f docker-bake.anihpj.hcl django-stack --push

Example 2: Environment-Specific Django Builds with Variable Overrides

Use bake variable overrides to build Django application for different environments (development, staging, production) with environment-specific configurations and optimizations.

# docker-bake.envs.hcl
variable "ENV" {
  default = "development"
}

variable "DEBUG" {
  default = "True"
}

variable "DJANGO_SECRET_KEY" {
  default = "dev-secret-key-not-for-production"
}

target "django-app" {
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.django-env"
  tags = ["anihpj/django-app:${ENV}"]
  platforms = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
  args = {
    DJANGO_ENV = ENV
    DJANGO_DEBUG = DEBUG
    DJANGO_SECRET_KEY = DJANGO_SECRET_KEY
    STATIC_FILES_STRATEGY = ENV == "production" ? "whitenoise" : "django.contrib.staticfiles"
  }
  target = ENV == "production" ? "production" : "development"
}

Build for development environment:

# Build development version with debug enabled
docker buildx bake -f docker-bake.envs.hcl \
  --set django-app.args.ENV=development \
  --set django-app.args.DEBUG=True \
  --load

Example 3: Skills API Microservice with Selective Baking

Build Skills API microservice with selective target baking for API server, background processors, and testing containers with shared base configurations.

# docker-bake.skills-api.hcl
variable "SKILLS_VERSION" {
  default = "v2.0"
}

group "skills-api" {
  targets = ["skills-server", "skills-processor", "skills-tester"]
}

group "skills-core" {
  targets = ["skills-server", "skills-processor"] 
}

target "skills-base" {
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.skills-base"
  args = {
    PYTHON_VERSION = "3.11"
    DJANGO_VERSION = "6.0"
    SKILLS_API_VERSION = SKILLS_VERSION
  }
}

target "skills-server" {
  inherits = ["skills-base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.skills-server"
  tags = ["anihpj/skills-api:${SKILLS_VERSION}"]
  platforms = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
  args = {
    API_PORT = "8080"
    API_WORKERS = "4"
  }
}

target "skills-processor" {
  inherits = ["skills-base"]  
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.skills-processor"
  tags = ["anihpj/skills-processor:${SKILLS_VERSION}"]
  platforms = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
  args = {
    PROCESSOR_CONCURRENCY = "8"
    BATCH_SIZE = "100"
  }
}

target "skills-tester" {
  inherits = ["skills-base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.skills-test"
  tags = ["anihpj/skills-tester:${SKILLS_VERSION}"]
  platforms = ["linux/amd64"]
  args = {
    TEST_FRAMEWORK = "pytest"
    COVERAGE_MIN = "85"
  }
}

Build only core Skills services (selective baking):

# Build only API server and processor (not tests)
docker buildx bake -f docker-bake.skills-api.hcl skills-core --push

Example 4: Location Service with Docker Compose Integration

Use Docker Compose file as bake source for Location service including PostGIS database, GeoServer, and location processing API with geographic data optimization.

# docker-compose.location.yml
version: '3.8'

x-location-base: &location-base
  build:
    context: .
    dockerfile: Dockerfile.location-base
    args:
      - POSTGIS_VERSION=15-3.3
      - GEOS_VERSION=3.11.0
  networks:
    - location-network
  environment:
    - DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE=anihpj.settings.geo

services:
  location-db:
    <<: *location-base
    build:
      dockerfile: Dockerfile.postgis
    image: anihpj/location-db:latest
    environment:
      - POSTGRES_DB=anihpj_geo
      - POSTGRES_USER=geouser  
      - POSTGRES_PASSWORD=geopass
    volumes:
      - location_data:/var/lib/postgresql/data
    ports:
      - "5433:5432"

  location-api:
    <<: *location-base
    build:
      dockerfile: Dockerfile.location-api
    image: anihpj/location-api:latest
    depends_on:
      - location-db
    ports:
      - "8090:8090"
    environment:
      - DATABASE_URL=postgis://geouser:geopass@location-db:5432/anihpj_geo
      - GDAL_LIBRARY_PATH=/usr/lib/libgdal.so

  geoserver:
    <<: *location-base  
    build:
      dockerfile: Dockerfile.geoserver
    image: anihpj/geoserver:latest
    depends_on:
      - location-db
    ports:
      - "8080:8080"
    environment:
      - GEOSERVER_ADMIN_PASSWORD=admin123
      - POSTGRES_CONNECTION=host=location-db,port=5432,database=anihpj_geo

  location-processor:
    <<: *location-base
    build:
      dockerfile: Dockerfile.location-processor
    image: anihpj/location-processor:latest
    depends_on:
      - location-db
      - location-api
    environment:
      - CELERY_BROKER_URL=redis://redis:6379/2
      - LOCATION_API_BASE=http://location-api:8090

networks:
  location-network:
    driver: bridge

volumes:
  location_data:

Location Model Geographic Operations:

# Test Location model with geographic capabilities
docker exec -it anihpj_location-api_1 python manage.py shell

from jobpost.models import Location, JobPost, Skills, Author, User
from django.contrib.gis.geos import Point, Polygon
from django.contrib.gis.measure import Distance
from django.db.models import Count, Q

# Geographic Location operations
print("Location Service - Geographic Analysis")
print(f"PostGIS enabled: {Location._meta.get_field('point').geographic}")

# Create bounding box for Bay Area
bay_area_box = Polygon.from_bbox((-122.5, 37.4, -122.1, 37.9))
bay_area_locations = Location.objects.filter(point__within=bay_area_box)

print(f"Bay Area Locations: {bay_area_locations.count()}")

# Location-based job analytics
location_stats = bay_area_locations.annotate(
    job_count=Count('jobpost'),
    remote_jobs=Count('jobpost', filter=Q(jobpost__remote_friendly=True))
).order_by('-job_count')

print("Location Job Distribution:")
for loc in location_stats[:5]:
    print(f"  {loc.name}: {loc.job_count} total, {loc.remote_jobs} remote")
    
# Distance-based queries
sf_center = Point(-122.4194, 37.7749, srid=4326)
nearby_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(
    location__point__distance_lte=(sf_center, Distance(km=25))
).select_related('location', 'author')

print(f"Jobs within 25km of SF: {nearby_jobs.count()}")
Location Service - Geographic Analysis PostGIS enabled: True Bay Area Locations: 8 Location Job Distribution: San Francisco: 245 total, 78 remote Oakland: 156 total, 45 remote San Jose: 189 total, 62 remote Berkeley: 89 total, 28 remote Palo Alto: 78 total, 34 remote Jobs within 25km of SF: 578 Location QuerySet: , , , , ]>
Example 5: Author Content Management with Advanced Inheritance

Build Author content management system using advanced bake inheritance patterns with shared base configurations, multi-stage optimizations, and content delivery networks.

# docker-bake.authors.hcl
variable "CDN_PROVIDER" {
  default = "cloudflare"
}

variable "CONTENT_CACHE_TTL" {
  default = "3600"
}

# Base configurations with inheritance
target "_base" {
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.base"
  args = {
    PYTHON_VERSION = "3.11"
    DJANGO_VERSION = "6.0"
    USER_ID = "1001"
    GROUP_ID = "1001"
  }
}

target "_django-base" {
  inherits = ["_base"]
  args = {
    DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE = "anihpj.settings.authors"
    STATIC_URL = "/static/"
    MEDIA_URL = "/media/"
  }
}

target "_content-base" {
  inherits = ["_django-base"]
  args = {
    CDN_PROVIDER = CDN_PROVIDER
    CACHE_TTL = CONTENT_CACHE_TTL
    CONTENT_COMPRESSION = "gzip"
  }
}

# Production targets with inheritance
target "author-api" {
  inherits = ["_content-base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.author-api"
  tags = ["anihpj/author-api:latest"]
  platforms = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
  target = "production"
  args = {
    API_VERSION = "v3"
    MAX_UPLOAD_SIZE = "50MB"
  }
}

target "content-processor" {
  inherits = ["_content-base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.content-processor"
  tags = ["anihpj/content-processor:latest"]
  platforms = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
  args = {
    PROCESSOR_TYPE = "multimedia"
    THUMBNAIL_SIZES = "150x150,300x300,600x600"
  }
}

target "content-cdn" {
  inherits = ["_base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.content-cdn"
  tags = ["anihpj/content-cdn:latest"]
  platforms = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
  args = {
    NGINX_VERSION = "1.24"
    CDN_PROVIDER = CDN_PROVIDER
    COMPRESSION_LEVEL = "6"
  }
}

target "author-worker" {
  inherits = ["_django-base"]
  dockerfile = "Dockerfile.author-worker"
  tags = ["anihpj/author-worker:latest"]
  platforms = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
  args = {
    CELERY_CONCURRENCY = "8"
    WORKER_TYPE = "content_processing"
  }
}

group "author-stack" {
  targets = ["author-api", "content-processor", "content-cdn", "author-worker"]
}

Build complete Author content management stack:

# Build Author stack with inheritance optimizations
docker buildx bake -f docker-bake.authors.hcl author-stack \
  --set author-api.args.CDN_PROVIDER=cloudflare \
  --set content-cdn.args.COMPRESSION_LEVEL=9 \
  --push

docker buildx create

Official Docs: docker buildx create | Docker CLI: docker buildx create

Create new builder instances with custom configurations for specialized Django build requirements, multi-platform support, and advanced BuildKit features.

Full Description

The docker buildx create command creates new builder instances that can be customized with specific drivers, platforms, and configurations tailored to your anihpj Django project's build requirements. Unlike the default docker builder, custom builders enable advanced BuildKit features, multi-platform builds, remote builder connections, and specialized build environments.

For Django development teams, custom builders are essential when you need to build for multiple architectures (ARM64 for Apple Silicon development, AMD64 for cloud deployment), use advanced caching strategies, connect to remote build clusters, or isolate builds between different projects or environments. Each builder instance can have its own configuration, supported platforms, and performance optimizations specific to Django application deployment scenarios.

Syntax

# Create basic builder instance
docker buildx create --name {builder-name}

# Create with specific driver
docker buildx create --name {builder-name} --driver {driver-type}

# Create with platform support
docker buildx create --name {builder-name} --platform {platforms}

# Create with remote node
docker buildx create --name {builder-name} {node-endpoint}

# Create with configuration
docker buildx create --name {builder-name} --config {config-file}

# Create and use immediately  
docker buildx create --name {builder-name} --use

# Create with driver options
docker buildx create --name {builder-name} --driver docker-container --driver-opt {option=value}

# Create with BuildKit image
docker buildx create --name {builder-name} --driver docker-container --driver-opt image={buildkit-image}

Parameters Description

  • --name: Builder instance name for identification and management. Must be unique across all builders for Django project organization and team coordination.
  • --driver: Builder driver type (docker, docker-container, kubernetes, remote). Each driver provides different capabilities for Django build scenarios and deployment environments.
  • --platform: Comma-separated list of supported platforms (linux/amd64, linux/arm64, etc.). Essential for Django cross-platform deployments and development team compatibility.
  • --use: Automatically switch to use the newly created builder. Streamlines Django development workflow by making the new builder immediately active.
  • --driver-opt: Driver-specific options for performance tuning and feature configuration. Optimizes Django build performance and enables specialized BuildKit features.
  • --config: Configuration file path for advanced builder settings. Enables team-wide Django build standardization and complex build environment setup.
  • --append: Add node to existing builder instead of creating new one. Useful for expanding Django build capacity or adding geographic build nodes.
  • --node: Node name for multi-node builders. Supports distributed Django builds across multiple machines or cloud regions.

Attributes

  • Builder Name: Unique identifier for the builder instance, used for management and team coordination in Django projects.
  • Driver Type: Determines builder capabilities, performance characteristics, and available features for Django builds.
  • Supported Platforms: List of architectures the builder can target for Django multi-platform deployments.
  • Node Configuration: Network endpoints, credentials, and connection details for distributed Django build scenarios.
  • Build Features: Available BuildKit features like cache mount, secret mount, SSH forwarding for advanced Django builds.

Methods

Create Multi-Platform Builder

Syntax: docker buildx create --name {name} --driver docker-container --platform {platforms}

Parameters: name (string) - Builder identifier, platforms (string) - Target architectures

Create builder instances capable of building Django applications for multiple architectures simultaneously.

Create Remote Builder Connection

Syntax: docker buildx create --name {name} --driver remote tcp://{host:port}

Parameters: name (string) - Builder identifier, host (string) - Remote BuildKit daemon endpoint

Connect to remote BuildKit instances for distributed Django builds and cloud-based build acceleration.

Create Kubernetes Builder

Syntax: docker buildx create --name {name} --driver kubernetes --driver-opt namespace={ns}

Parameters: name (string) - Builder identifier, namespace (string) - Kubernetes namespace

Create builders that run Django builds as Kubernetes jobs for scalable container orchestration.

Return Value

Returns builder instance identifier and configuration details upon successful creation. Provides builder name, driver type, and initial status information. Failed creations return specific error messages about configuration issues or connectivity problems.

  • Success (0): Builder created successfully with valid configuration
  • Error (1): Creation failed due to invalid parameters or connectivity issues
  • Error (2): Driver initialization error or platform incompatibility

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Development Team Multi-Platform Builder

Create a specialized builder for Django development team supporting both Apple Silicon (ARM64) and Intel (AMD64) development environments with optimized caching for Skills API development.

# Create development team builder with multi-platform support
docker buildx create \
    --name anihpj-dev-team \
    --driver docker-container \
    --platform linux/amd64,linux/arm64,darwin/amd64,darwin/arm64 \
    --driver-opt network=host \
    --use
anihpj-dev-team
# Inspect the created builder
docker buildx inspect anihpj-dev-team --bootstrap

Example 2: Production CI/CD Builder with Advanced Caching

Create a production-optimized builder for CI/CD pipelines with registry cache, secret management, and build performance optimization for User authentication service deployment.

# Create production CI/CD builder with advanced features
docker buildx create \
    --name anihpj-production-ci \
    --driver docker-container \
    --driver-opt image=moby/buildkit:v0.12.4-rootless \
    --driver-opt cache-from=type=registry,ref=anihpj/buildcache:ci \
    --driver-opt cache-to=type=registry,ref=anihpj/buildcache:ci \
    --platform linux/amd64,linux/arm64
anihpj-production-ci
# Configure production builder with build secrets
echo "DJANGO_SECRET_KEY=prod-secret-12345" > .env.prod
echo "DATABASE_PASSWORD=secure-db-pass" >> .env.prod
echo "REDIS_PASSWORD=cache-secure-pass" >> .env.prod
# Use production builder for User authentication deployment
docker buildx use anihpj-production-ci

# Build User auth with secrets and optimizations
docker buildx build \
    --secret id=prod-env,src=.env.prod \
    --cache-from type=registry,ref=anihpj/buildcache:user-auth \
    --cache-to type=registry,ref=anihpj/buildcache:user-auth,mode=max \
    --platform linux/amd64,linux/arm64 \
    -t anihpj/user-auth:prod-v2.1 \
    --push \
    --target production \
    -f Dockerfile.user-auth-secure .

Example 3: Kubernetes-Based Builder for Author Content Processing

Create a Kubernetes builder for Author content processing that runs builds as Kubernetes jobs, enabling auto-scaling and distributed builds for content management workflows.

# Create Kubernetes builder for Author content processing
docker buildx create \
    --name anihpj-k8s-content \
    --driver kubernetes \
    --driver-opt namespace=anihpj-builds \
    --driver-opt replicas=3 \
    --driver-opt requests.cpu=1000m \
    --driver-opt requests.memory=2Gi \
    --driver-opt limits.cpu=2000m \
    --driver-opt limits.memory=4Gi
anihpj-k8s-content
# Verify Kubernetes builder setup
kubectl get pods -n anihpj-builds
kubectl get jobs -n anihpj-builds

Deploy Author content processor:

# Deploy on Kubernetes cluster
kubectl apply -f - << EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: author-content-processor
  namespace: anihpj-content
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: author-content-processor
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: author-content-processor
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: processor
        image: anihpj/author-content-processor:k8s-v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8080
        env:
        - name: CONTENT_WORKERS
          value: "6"
        - name: KUBERNETES_BUILD
          value: "true"
        resources:
          requests:
            cpu: 500m
            memory: 1Gi
          limits:
            cpu: 1000m
            memory: 2Gi
EOF
deployment.apps/author-content-processor created

# Advanced geographic queries with remote optimization

# Complex spatial analytics

    job_count=Count('jobpost'),
    tech_job_count=Count('jobpost', filter=Q(jobpost__skills__category='Programming')),
    avg_distance_to_center=Distance('point', Point(-122.4194, 37.7749))
).order_by('avg_distance_to_center')

print("Geographic Job Distribution (Remote GIS):")

print(f"Parallel Processing: Enabled on 32-core cluster")

Example 5: Specialized JobPost Analytics Builder with Custom Configuration

Create a specialized builder for JobPost analytics processing with custom configuration file, performance tuning, and machine learning model builds requiring specialized compute resources.

Create custom builder configuration:

# buildx-config.jobpost-analytics.toml
[worker.oci]
  max-parallelism = 8
  
[worker.containerd]
  enabled = true
  platforms = ["linux/amd64", "linux/arm64"]
  
[registry."anihpj.azurecr.io"]
  mirrors = ["anihpj-cache.azurecr.io"]
  
[grpc]
  address = ["unix:///var/run/buildkit/buildkitd.sock"]
  
[cache.registry]
  enabled = true
  ref = "anihpj.azurecr.io/buildcache/jobpost-analytics"
  
[frontend.dockerfile.v0]
  enabled = true
  
[frontend.gateway.v0]
  enabled = true
# Create JobPost analytics builder with custom config
docker buildx create \
    --name anihpj-jobpost-analytics \
    --driver docker-container \
    --config ./buildx-config.jobpost-analytics.toml \
    --driver-opt image=moby/buildkit:v0.12.4 \
    --driver-opt cache-from=type=registry,ref=anihpj.azurecr.io/buildcache/analytics \
    --driver-opt cache-to=type=registry,ref=anihpj.azurecr.io/buildcache/analytics \
    --platform linux/amd64,linux/arm64
anihpj-jobpost-analytics

JobPost Model ML Analytics Operations:

# Test JobPost model with ML analytics builder
docker exec -it jobpost-analytics-ml python manage.py shell

from jobpost.models import JobPost, Skills, Author, Location, User
from django.db.models import Count, Avg, Q, F
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestRegressor
import numpy as np
import os

# ML Analytics environment
print("JobPost Analytics - ML Builder Configuration")
print(f"ML Models: {os.getenv('ML_MODELS_ENABLED', 'true')}")
print(f"Analytics Workers: {os.getenv('ANALYTICS_WORKERS', '8')}")
print(f"Builder: anihpj-jobpost-analytics (custom config)")

# JobPost ML feature engineering
ml_features = JobPost.objects.select_related('location', 'author').prefetch_related('skills').annotate(
    skills_count=Count('skills'),
    location_job_density=Count('location__jobpost'),
    author_experience=Count('author__jobpost')
).filter(salary_max__isnull=False, salary_min__isnull=False)

print(f"ML Training Dataset: {ml_features.count()} jobs")

# Advanced analytics queries
salary_analytics = ml_features.aggregate(
    avg_salary=Avg(F('salary_min') + F('salary_max')) / 2,
    min_salary=Min('salary_min'),
    max_salary=Max('salary_max'),
    skill_diversity=Avg('skills_count')
)

print("Salary Analytics:")
for metric, value in salary_analytics.items():
    print(f"  {metric}: {value:.2f}" if isinstance(value, float) else f"  {metric}: {value}")

# ML model performance simulation
high_demand_skills = Skills.objects.filter(demand_score__gte=85)
print(f"High-Demand Skills for ML: {high_demand_skills.count()}")

for skill in high_demand_skills[:5]:
    job_count = JobPost.objects.filter(skills=skill).count()
    print(f"  {skill.name}: {job_count} jobs (demand: {skill.demand_score})")

docker buildx imagetools

Official Docs: docker buildx imagetools | Docker CLI: docker buildx imagetools

Inspect and manipulate multi-platform container images and manifests for advanced Django deployment scenarios, registry management, and cross-platform compatibility verification.

Full Description

The docker buildx imagetools command provides advanced image inspection and manipulation capabilities for multi-platform container images. For your anihpj Django project, imagetools is essential when managing complex deployment scenarios involving multiple architectures, validating cross-platform builds, creating custom multi-platform manifests, and troubleshooting registry-related issues.

Imagetools enables Django development teams to inspect manifest lists, verify platform-specific image layers, create custom multi-platform images from existing single-platform builds, and manage registry metadata. This is particularly valuable for Django applications deployed across different cloud providers, development environments with mixed architectures (Intel and ARM), and CI/CD pipelines requiring detailed image validation and manipulation.

Syntax

# Inspect multi-platform image manifest
docker buildx imagetools inspect {image-ref}

# Create multi-platform manifest from existing images
docker buildx imagetools create -t {target-ref} {source-ref1} {source-ref2}

# Inspect specific platform image
docker buildx imagetools inspect --format json {image-ref}

# Create manifest with specific tags
docker buildx imagetools create -t {target}:latest -t {target}:v1.0 {source}

# Inspect and extract platform details
docker buildx imagetools inspect --raw {image-ref}

# Create from multi-platform sources
docker buildx imagetools create -t {target} {source}@{digest1} {source}@{digest2}

# Inspect with custom output format
docker buildx imagetools inspect --format '{{ .Manifest.MediaType }}' {image-ref}

Parameters Description

  • inspect: Display detailed information about image manifests, platforms, and metadata. Essential for Django deployment validation and troubleshooting multi-platform builds.
  • create: Create new multi-platform manifests by combining existing images. Useful for Django applications when building platform-specific images separately and combining them.
  • -t, --tag: Tag names for the created manifest. Supports multiple tags for Django versioning strategies and deployment environment labeling.
  • --format: Output format for inspect command (json, raw, or template). Enables automated Django deployment pipeline integration and custom analysis tools.
  • --raw: Display raw manifest JSON without formatting. Provides complete manifest details for Django deployment automation and registry debugging.
  • --dry-run: Show what would be created without actually creating the manifest. Useful for Django deployment validation and testing manifest creation logic.
  • --append: Add platform images to existing multi-platform manifest instead of replacing. Enables incremental Django multi-platform deployment strategies.
  • --platform: Filter inspect output to specific platforms. Helps Django teams focus on relevant architecture-specific information during deployment verification.

Attributes

  • Manifest Type: Identifies whether image is single-platform or multi-platform manifest list for Django deployment planning.
  • Platform Details: Architecture, OS, and variant information for each platform in Django cross-platform deployments.
  • Layer Information: Digests, sizes, and metadata for image layers enabling Django deployment optimization and troubleshooting.
  • Registry Metadata: Creation time, labels, annotations, and other registry-specific information for Django image management.
  • Digest References: Immutable content-addressable identifiers for precise Django deployment targeting and version control.

Methods

Inspect Multi-Platform Manifest

Syntax: docker buildx imagetools inspect {image-ref}

Parameters: image-ref (string) - Registry reference to multi-platform image

Analyze Django application images for platform compatibility, layer structure, and deployment readiness across architectures.

Create Combined Manifest

Syntax: docker buildx imagetools create -t {target} {source1} {source2}

Parameters: target (string) - New manifest reference, sources (strings) - Platform-specific image references

Combine separately built Django platform images into unified multi-platform deployment manifest for registry distribution.

Extract Platform-Specific Image

Syntax: docker buildx imagetools inspect --platform {platform} {image-ref}

Parameters: platform (string) - Target platform specification, image-ref (string) - Multi-platform image reference

Extract specific platform details from Django multi-platform images for targeted deployment and debugging scenarios.

Return Value

Returns detailed manifest information, platform specifications, and image metadata. For inspect operations, provides manifest structure, layer details, and platform availability. Create operations return new manifest digest and reference information.

  • Success (0): Operation completed successfully with valid manifest data
  • Error (1): Image not found or insufficient permissions for registry access
  • Error (2): Invalid manifest format or corrupted image data

Example 2: User Authentication Service Manifest Creation

Create a unified multi-platform manifest for User authentication service by combining separately built platform-specific images for optimal CI/CD pipeline integration and deployment flexibility.

Build platform-specific User auth images separately:

# Build AMD64 version for cloud deployment
docker buildx build --platform linux/amd64 \
    -t anihpj/user-auth:amd64-only \
    --push -f Dockerfile.user-auth .

# Build ARM64 version for Apple Silicon development  
docker buildx build --platform linux/arm64 \
    -t anihpj/user-auth:arm64-only \
    --push -f Dockerfile.user-auth .
[AMD64 Build] [+] Building 32.4s (18/18) FINISHED => pushing layers 6.2s => pushing manifest for docker.io/anihpj/user-auth:amd64-only 0.3s [ARM64 Build] [+] Building 35.7s (18/18) FINISHED => pushing layers 7.1s => pushing manifest for docker.io/anihpj/user-auth:arm64-only 0.3s

Create unified multi-platform manifest:

# Combine platform-specific images into multi-platform manifest
docker buildx imagetools create \
    -t anihpj/user-auth:unified-v2.0 \
    -t anihpj/user-auth:latest \
    anihpj/user-auth:amd64-only \
    anihpj/user-auth:arm64-only
anihpj/user-auth:unified-v2.0 anihpj/user-auth:latest

Location Model Geographic Platform Analysis:

# Analyze Location model with geographic platform optimization
docker exec -it location-global python manage.py shell

from jobpost.models import Location, JobPost, Skills, Author, User
from django.contrib.gis.geos import Point
from django.contrib.gis.measure import Distance  
from django.db.models import Count, Q
import platform
import os

# Geographic platform analysis
print(f"Global Location Service Platform: {platform.machine()}")
print(f"Geographic Region: {os.getenv('GEOGRAPHIC_REGION', 'auto')}")
print(f"Deployment Zone: {os.getenv('DEPLOYMENT_ZONE', 'adaptive')}")

# Location distribution analysis
global_locations = Location.objects.annotate(
    job_count=Count('jobpost'),
    remote_jobs=Count('jobpost', filter=Q(jobpost__remote_friendly=True)),
    tech_jobs=Count('jobpost', filter=Q(jobpost__skills__category='Programming'))
).filter(job_count__gt=0)

print(f"Global Locations: {global_locations.count()}")

# Geographic clustering analysis
us_locations = global_locations.filter(
    point__longitude__lte=-100  # Rough US boundary
)
eu_locations = global_locations.filter(
    point__longitude__gte=0,
    point__longitude__lte=30,  # Rough EU boundary  
    point__latitude__gte=40,
    point__latitude__lte=60
)

print("Geographic Distribution:")
print(f"  US Locations: {us_locations.count()}")  
print(f"  EU Locations: {eu_locations.count()}")

# Platform-optimized location queries
print("Top Locations by Region:")
for region, qs in [("US", us_locations), ("EU", eu_locations)]:
    top_locations = qs.order_by('-job_count')[:3]
    print(f"  {region}:")
    for loc in top_locations:
        print(f"    {loc.name}: {loc.job_count} jobs ({loc.remote_jobs} remote)")
