docker compose restart

Official Docs: docker compose restart | Docker CLI: docker compose restart

Restart running services to apply configuration changes and refresh service state.

Full Description

The docker compose restart command stops and starts existing containers for your anihpj Django services. This is useful for applying environment variable changes, refreshing service connections, clearing temporary states, and implementing configuration updates without full container recreation.

For Django applications, restarting services helps apply new settings, refresh database connections, reload application code (in development), clear cache states, and resolve temporary networking or performance issues in your anihpj jobpost application stack.

Syntax

# Restart all services
docker compose restart

# Restart specific service
docker compose restart web

# Restart with timeout
docker compose restart --timeout 30 web

# Restart multiple services
docker compose restart web db redis

# Restart with no timeout (immediate)
docker compose restart --timeout 0 worker

# Sequential restart of services
docker compose restart db && docker compose restart web

# Restart all except specific services
docker compose restart $(docker compose ps --services | grep -v db)

Parameters Description

  • -t, --timeout: Set stop timeout in seconds before force killing. Allows Django applications to complete current requests gracefully.
  • Service Names: Specify which Django services to restart. Target specific components without affecting entire stack.
  • Multiple Services: Restart several related Django services together. Coordinate database, cache, and web service restarts.
  • Zero Timeout: Immediate restart without graceful shutdown. Use for Django services that need immediate state reset.
  • Dependency Order: Restart services in dependency order. Ensure Django database services start before web applications.

Attributes

  • State Preservation: Maintains container configuration while refreshing Django service processes and connections.
  • Network Continuity: Preserves Django service networking and inter-service communication during restart cycles.
  • Volume Persistence: Django data volumes remain intact during restart operations, preserving database and file states.
  • Graceful Shutdown: Allows Django applications to complete in-flight requests before stopping services.
  • Quick Recovery: Faster than full recreation, ideal for Django configuration updates and state refreshes.

Methods

Configuration Refresh

Syntax: docker compose restart --timeout 60

Parameters: --timeout (integer) - Grace period for Django application shutdown

Apply Django configuration changes with graceful restart allowing current operations to complete safely.

Service Health Reset

Syntax: docker compose restart db redis web

Parameters: Service list in dependency order for Django stack restart

Reset Django service health by restarting in proper dependency sequence for optimal recovery.

Return Value

Returns restart status for each Django service showing stop and start completion. Indicates any failures during restart cycles.

  • Success (0): All specified services restarted successfully
  • Error (1): Service restart failure or timeout issues
  • Partial Success: Some services restarted, others failed

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Production Configuration Refresh (Environment Variables Update)

Scenario: Applying new Django environment variables and configuration changes to production services without full downtime, affecting User authentication and JobPost functionality.

# Restart web services with new configuration
docker compose restart --timeout 60 web

# Restart background workers for job processing
docker compose restart worker scheduler

# Verify restart success and health
docker compose ps

    area_name = config_area.replace('_', ' ').title()
    print(f"\n   📊 {area_name}:")

    for change in details['changes']:
        print(f"      - {change}")

total_estimated_downtime = 0
for phase, details in service_restart_plan.items():
    phase_name = phase.replace('_', ' ').title()
    downtime_seconds = int(details['estimated_downtime'].split()[0])
    total_estimated_downtime += downtime_seconds
    
    print(f"\n   🔄 {phase_name}:")

    print(f"      Downtime: {details['estimated_downtime']}")
    print(f"      Operations affected: {', '.join(details['affected_operations'])}")

for model_name, operations in model_operations.items():
    critical_ops = sum(1 for op in operations.values() if op['critical'])
    total_ops = len(operations)
    
    print(f"\n   🎯 {model_name} Model:")
    print(f"      Critical operations: {critical_ops}/{total_ops}")
    
    for operation, details in operations.items():
        critical_indicator = "🔴" if details['critical'] else "🟡"
        fallback_strategy = details['fallback'].replace('_', ' ').title()
        op_name = operation.replace('_', ' ').title()
        
        print(f"      {critical_indicator} {op_name}: Fallback = {fallback_strategy}")

# Restart execution simulation

    print(f"   {status_icon} {service}: {result['status']} in {result['time']} {health_icon}")

actual_total_time = sum(float(result["time"].replace("s", "")) for result in restart_results.values())

docker compose stop

Official Docs: docker compose stop | Docker CLI: docker compose stop

Stop running services gracefully without removing containers or losing data.

Full Description

The docker compose stop command gracefully stops running containers for your anihpj Django services without removing them or their data. This preserves container state, volumes, and configuration while halting service execution, making it perfect for maintenance windows, temporary shutdowns, or resource conservation.

For Django applications, stopping services maintains database data, preserves session information, keeps configuration intact, and allows for quick restart without container recreation. This is essential for planned maintenance, system updates, or temporary resource management in your anihpj jobpost application environment.

Syntax

# Stop all services
docker compose stop

# Stop specific service
docker compose stop web

# Stop with custom timeout
docker compose stop --timeout 60 web

# Stop multiple services
docker compose stop web worker db

# Stop immediately (no graceful shutdown)
docker compose stop --timeout 0 worker

# Stop services in reverse dependency order
docker compose stop web && docker compose stop db

# Stop all except specific services  
docker compose stop $(docker compose ps --services | grep -v redis)

Parameters Description

  • -t, --timeout: Set stop timeout before force kill. Allows Django applications to finish current requests and close connections gracefully.
  • Service Names: Specify which Django services to stop. Target specific components while keeping others running.
  • Zero Timeout: Immediate stop without graceful shutdown. Use for Django services that need immediate halting.
  • Multiple Services: Stop several Django services together. Coordinate shutdown of related application components.
  • Dependency Order: Stop services in proper sequence. Halt Django web services before stopping database dependencies.

Attributes

  • Container Preservation: Stops Django services without removing containers, maintaining configuration and state for restart.
  • Data Persistence: Preserves all Django database data, uploaded files, and application state during shutdown.
  • Graceful Shutdown: Allows Django applications to complete in-flight operations before stopping services.
  • Quick Recovery: Enables fast restart with preserved state, ideal for Django maintenance and updates.
  • Resource Management: Frees CPU and memory while maintaining Django service configuration and data.

Methods

Maintenance Window

Syntax: docker compose stop --timeout 120

Parameters: --timeout (integer) - Extended grace period for Django application shutdown

Initiate Django maintenance window with extended graceful shutdown for complex operations completion.

Selective Service Shutdown

Syntax: docker compose stop web worker

Parameters: Service list for selective Django component shutdown

Stop Django application services while keeping database and cache running for data consistency.

Return Value

Returns stop status for each Django service showing graceful shutdown completion. Indicates timeout or force-stop situations.

  • Success (0): All specified services stopped gracefully
  • Timeout: Services stopped after timeout period elapsed
  • Error (1): Service stop failure or container access issues

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Scheduled Maintenance Window (Graceful System Shutdown)

Scenario: Implementing planned maintenance window for Django system updates, database optimization, and security patches while preserving all data and configurations.

docker compose stop --timeout 180

# Check stop status and verify data preservation
docker compose ps -a

# Verify data volumes are intact
docker volume ls | grep anihpj

docker compose start

Official Docs: docker compose start | Docker CLI: docker compose start

Start existing stopped containers to resume Django services with preserved state.

Full Description

The docker compose start command starts previously stopped containers for your anihpj Django services. Unlike 'up', this command only starts existing containers without creating new ones, preserving all previous configurations, data states, and service relationships from before the shutdown.

For Django applications, starting stopped services restores your application stack to its previous state, reconnects to existing databases, resumes job processing, and continues serving user requests exactly where it left off. This is perfect for resuming after maintenance windows, system reboots, or planned downtime in your anihpj jobpost application environment.

Syntax

# Start all stopped services
docker compose start

# Start specific service
docker compose start web

# Start multiple services
docker compose start web db redis

# Start services in dependency order
docker compose start db && docker compose start web

# Start with verification
docker compose start && docker compose ps

# Start and follow logs
docker compose start && docker compose logs -f

# Start all except specific services
docker compose start $(docker compose ps --services --filter status=exited | grep -v worker)

Parameters Description

  • Service Names: Specify which Django services to start. Target specific components for selective restoration.
  • Multiple Services: Start several related Django services together. Coordinate database, cache, and application service startup.
  • Dependency Order: Start services in proper sequence. Ensure Django database services start before web applications.
  • State Preservation: Maintains all Django service configuration and data from before shutdown.
  • Quick Recovery: Fast startup since containers already exist with preserved Django application state.

Attributes

  • Container Reuse: Uses existing Django containers with preserved configuration, environment variables, and mount points.
  • State Continuity: Maintains Django application state including database connections, cache entries, and session data.
  • Fast Startup: Quick service restoration without image pulling or container creation for Django applications.
  • Data Integrity: Preserves all Django model data, uploaded files, and application state from before shutdown.
  • Network Preservation: Maintains Django service networking and inter-service communication configuration.

Methods

Post-Maintenance Startup

Syntax: docker compose start db && sleep 10 && docker compose start web

Parameters: Staged startup with delay for Django database initialization

Resume Django services after maintenance with proper dependency startup sequence for optimal recovery.

Selective Service Recovery

Syntax: docker compose start web redis

Parameters: Specific service list for selective Django component restoration

Start critical Django services while keeping other components stopped for testing or resource management.

Return Value

Returns start status for each Django service showing successful restoration. Indicates any startup failures or dependency issues.

  • Success (0): All specified services started successfully
  • Error (1): Service start failure or container access issues
  • Dependency Errors: Required services not running for Django application startup

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Post-Maintenance Recovery (Complete System Restoration)

Scenario: Restoring Django application stack after scheduled maintenance, ensuring all models and services resume with preserved data and optimal startup sequence.

# Start database first for Django models
docker compose start db

# Wait for database readiness, then start web services  
sleep 15 && docker compose start web worker

# Verify all services are healthy
docker compose ps && docker compose logs --tail 50

docker compose pause

Official Docs: docker compose pause | Docker CLI: docker compose pause

Suspend Django service processes while preserving memory state and container configuration.

Full Description

The docker compose pause command suspends all processes in your anihpj Django service containers without stopping them completely. This freezes the current state in memory including active connections, loaded data, and running processes, making it perfect for temporary resource conservation, testing scenarios, or system inspection without service disruption.

For Django applications, pausing services maintains application state, preserves database connections, keeps sessions active, and allows for instant resumption without restart overhead. This is useful for debugging, resource management, testing deployments, or temporary system isolation in your anihpj jobpost application environment.

Syntax

# Pause all services
docker compose pause

# Pause specific service
docker compose pause web

# Pause multiple services  
docker compose pause web worker

# Pause all except critical services
docker compose pause $(docker compose ps --services | grep -v db)

# Pause with verification
docker compose pause && docker compose ps

# Pause for debugging session
docker compose pause web && docker exec -it anihpj_db_1 psql

# Pause worker services only
docker compose pause worker scheduler

Parameters Description

  • Service Names: Specify which Django services to pause. Target specific components while keeping others active.
  • Multiple Services: Pause several related Django services together. Coordinate suspension of application components.
  • Selective Pausing: Keep critical Django services running while suspending others for testing or resource management.
  • State Preservation: Maintains all Django application state in memory during pause period.
  • Instant Resumption: Enables immediate service restoration without startup delays for Django applications.

Attributes

  • Memory Preservation: Maintains Django application memory state including loaded models, cached data, and active sessions.
  • Process Suspension: Freezes Django service processes without termination, preserving execution context and state.
  • Resource Conservation: Reduces CPU usage while maintaining Django service availability for instant resumption.
  • Connection Maintenance: Preserves Django database connections and inter-service communication channels during pause.
  • Zero Restart Overhead: Instant service resumption without Django application startup or initialization delays.

Methods

Debug Session Preparation

Syntax: docker compose pause web worker

Parameters: Service list for Django component suspension during debugging

Suspend Django application services while keeping database active for safe debugging and inspection.

Resource Conservation

Syntax: docker compose pause $(docker compose ps --services | grep -v critical)

Parameters: Filtered service list excluding critical Django infrastructure

Pause non-essential Django services to conserve system resources while maintaining core functionality.

Return Value

Returns pause status for each Django service showing successful suspension. Indicates any failures during pause operations.

  • Success (0): All specified services paused successfully
  • Error (1): Service pause failure or container access issues
  • Partial Success: Some services paused, others failed or already paused

5 Practical Django Examples

docker compose unpause

Official Docs: docker compose unpause | Docker CLI: docker compose unpause

Resume paused Django service processes with preserved memory state and instant restoration.

Full Description

The docker compose unpause command resumes previously paused containers for your anihpj Django services. This instantly restores all processes from their suspended state, maintaining memory contents, active connections, loaded data, and execution context exactly as they were before pausing.

For Django applications, unpausing services provides zero-downtime restoration, maintains session continuity, preserves database connection pools, and resumes background job processing without any initialization overhead. This is perfect for completing debugging sessions, finishing performance tests, or restoring full functionality after temporary resource conservation in your anihpj jobpost application environment.

Syntax

# Unpause all paused services
docker compose unpause

# Unpause specific service
docker compose unpause web

# Unpause multiple services
docker compose unpause web worker

# Unpause with verification
docker compose unpause && docker compose ps

# Unpause and monitor logs
docker compose unpause worker && docker compose logs -f worker

# Unpause background services only
docker compose unpause worker scheduler

# Unpause all except specific services  
docker compose unpause $(docker compose ps --filter status=paused --format="{{.Service}}" | grep -v critical)

Parameters Description

  • Service Names: Specify which Django services to unpause. Target specific components for selective restoration.
  • Multiple Services: Resume several related Django services together. Coordinate restoration of application components.
  • Selective Unpausing: Resume specific Django services while keeping others paused for continued testing or resource management.
  • State Restoration: Instantly restores Django application state from exactly where it was paused.
  • Zero Overhead: Immediate service resumption without Django application startup or initialization delays.

Attributes

  • Instant Restoration: Resumes Django services immediately with all memory state, connections, and processes intact from pause point.
  • Memory Continuity: Maintains Django application memory contents including cached data, loaded models, and active sessions.
  • Process Resumption: Restarts Django service processes from exact suspension point without losing execution context.
  • Connection Preservation: Maintains Django database connections and inter-service communication channels established before pause.
  • Session Continuity: Preserves Django user sessions and application state for seamless user experience restoration.

Methods

Post-Debug Restoration

Syntax: docker compose unpause web worker

Parameters: Service list for Django component restoration after debugging

Resume Django application services after debugging session with preserved state for continued development work.

Selective Service Activation

Syntax: docker compose unpause worker && sleep 5 && docker compose unpause scheduler

Parameters: Staged unpausing with delay for Django service coordination

Resume Django background services in sequence to ensure proper job processing queue restoration and task coordination.

Return Value

Returns unpause status for each Django service showing successful resumption. Indicates any failures during unpause operations or services not in paused state.

  • Success (0): All specified services unpaused successfully
  • Error (1): Service unpause failure or container access issues
  • Warning: Service not in paused state or already running

5 Practical Django Examples

# Verify service restoration and queue status
docker compose ps && docker compose logs --tail 20 worker

# Monitor job processing resumption
docker compose exec worker celery -A anihpj inspect active

docker compose kill

Official Docs: docker compose kill | Docker CLI: docker compose kill

Force terminate Django service containers immediately without graceful shutdown.

Full Description

The docker compose kill command forcefully terminates running containers for your anihpj Django services without allowing graceful shutdown procedures. This sends a SIGKILL signal (or specified signal) to containers, immediately stopping all processes without cleanup, data flushing, or connection closing.

For Django applications, this command should be used sparingly and only in emergency situations such as unresponsive services, infinite loops, deadlocked processes, or when immediate termination is required. It bypasses Django's normal shutdown procedures and may result in data inconsistency, incomplete transactions, or corrupted temporary files in your anihpj jobpost application environment.

Syntax

# Kill all services (SIGKILL)
docker compose kill

# Kill specific service
docker compose kill web

# Kill with specific signal
docker compose kill -s SIGTERM web

# Kill multiple services
docker compose kill web worker

# Kill with SIGINT (Ctrl+C equivalent)
docker compose kill -s SIGINT worker

# Kill immediately without signal options
docker compose kill --signal KILL db

# Emergency kill all except critical services
docker compose kill $(docker compose ps --services | grep -v db)

Parameters Description

  • -s, --signal: Signal to send to Django containers (SIGKILL, SIGTERM, SIGINT). Choose signal type based on emergency termination requirements.
  • Service Names: Specify which Django services to kill. Target problematic components without affecting stable services.
  • Multiple Services: Force terminate several Django services together. Emergency shutdown of related application components.
  • Signal Types: SIGKILL (immediate), SIGTERM (terminate), SIGINT (interrupt) for different Django termination scenarios.
  • Emergency Use: Last resort for Django services that don't respond to normal stop commands.

Attributes

  • Immediate Termination: Instantly stops Django service processes without waiting for graceful shutdown procedures.
  • No Cleanup: Bypasses Django application cleanup routines, potentially leaving temporary files or incomplete transactions.
  • Signal Control: Allows sending specific termination signals to Django containers based on emergency requirements.
  • Emergency Response: Designed for Django service recovery when normal stop procedures fail or hang indefinitely.
  • Data Risk: May cause Django data inconsistency or corruption due to abrupt process termination without proper cleanup.

Methods

Emergency Service Recovery

Syntax: docker compose kill -s SIGTERM web && docker compose start web

Parameters: --signal SIGTERM (terminate signal) for Django service emergency restart

Force terminate unresponsive Django web service and restart for immediate recovery from deadlock or infinite loop conditions.

Selective Process Termination

Syntax: docker compose kill -s SIGINT worker

Parameters: --signal SIGINT (interrupt signal) for Django background service termination

Send interrupt signal to Django background worker experiencing processing issues while preserving other services.

Return Value

Returns kill status for each Django service showing immediate termination completion. No graceful shutdown status since processes are forcefully terminated.

  • Success (0): All specified services killed successfully
  • Error (1): Service kill failure or container access issues
  • Warning: Service already stopped or not responding to kill signals

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Emergency Deadlock Recovery (Unresponsive Database Connection)

Scenario: Django web service deadlocked on database operations affecting User authentication and JobPost creation, requiring immediate termination and recovery.

# Emergency kill unresponsive web service
docker compose kill -s SIGTERM web

# Check for data corruption and restart
docker compose exec db psql -U postgres -c "SELECT COUNT(*) FROM pg_stat_activity;"

# Restart web service with fresh state
docker compose start web

        print(f"        - {operation.replace('_', ' ').title()}")
    
    if 'users_affected' in details:
        print(f"      Users affected: {details['users_affected']}")
    if 'timeout_errors' in details:
        print(f"      Timeout errors: {details['timeout_errors']}")

print(f"\n💾 Database Status During Deadlock:")
conn_pool = database_status['connection_pool']
print(f"   Connection pool: {conn_pool['active_connections']}/{conn_pool['max_connections']} used")
print(f"   Waiting queries: {conn_pool['waiting_queries']}")
print(f"   Deadlocked transactions: {conn_pool['deadlocked_transactions']}")

perf = database_status['performance_impact']
print(f"\n   Performance impact:")
print(f"     Query wait time: {perf['query_wait_time']}")
print(f"     Timeout rate: {perf['connection_timeout_rate']}")
print(f"     CPU usage: {perf['cpu_usage']}")

print(f"\n⚡ Emergency Kill Decision:")
print(f"   Normal stop attempted: {kill_decision['normal_stop_attempted']}")
print(f"   Stop duration: {kill_decision['normal_stop_duration']}")
print(f"   Success: {kill_decision['stop_success']}")
print(f"   Selected signal: {kill_decision['signal_selection']}")

print(f"\n   Justification:")
for reason in kill_decision['kill_justification']:
    print(f"     - {reason}")

print(f"\n🛡️ Data Integrity Assessment:")
for model, integrity in data_integrity.items():
    if model != "database_state":
        model_name = model.replace('_', ' ')
        print(f"\n   📋 {model_name}:")
        print(f"      At-risk operations: {len(integrity['at_risk_operations'])}")
        print(f"      Mitigation: {integrity['mitigation_strategy'].replace('_', ' ').title()}")
        print(f"      Expected loss: {integrity['expected_data_loss'].replace('_', ' ').title()}")

# Simulate emergency kill execution

    "signal_sent": "SIGTERM",

for action_category, actions in recovery_procedure.items():

    for action in actions:
        print(f"     - {action.replace('_', ' ').title()}")

docker compose rm

Official Docs: docker compose rm | Docker CLI: docker compose rm

Remove stopped Django service containers while preserving volumes and images for cleanup.

Full Description

The docker compose rm command removes stopped containers for your anihpj Django services without affecting running containers, volumes, or images. This cleans up container instances that have exited, freeing disk space and maintaining a clean environment while preserving important data and configurations.

For Django applications, removing stopped containers helps maintain system hygiene, frees storage space, prevents container name conflicts, and ensures clean environment management. This is essential for development workflows, CI/CD pipelines, and production maintenance in your anihpj jobpost application environment.

Syntax

# Remove all stopped services
docker compose rm

# Remove specific stopped service
docker compose rm web

# Remove without confirmation prompt
docker compose rm -f

# Remove with volumes (DANGEROUS)
docker compose rm -v

# Remove stopped services and anonymous volumes
docker compose rm -f -v

# Remove multiple specific services
docker compose rm web worker

# List what would be removed
docker compose rm --dry-run

Parameters Description

  • -f, --force: Remove without confirmation prompt. Essential for Django automated deployment scripts and CI/CD pipelines.
  • -v, --volumes: Remove anonymous volumes attached to containers. WARNING: This deletes Django database and file data permanently.
  • Service Names: Specify which stopped Django services to remove. Target specific components for selective cleanup.
  • --dry-run: Show what would be removed without actually removing. Preview Django container cleanup before execution.
  • Multiple Services: Remove several stopped Django services together. Batch cleanup of related application components.

Attributes

  • Container Cleanup: Removes only stopped Django containers, ensuring running services remain unaffected during cleanup.
  • Volume Preservation: By default preserves Django data volumes and named volumes, protecting database and file data.
  • Selective Removal: Allows targeting specific Django services for container cleanup without affecting entire stack.
  • Storage Recovery: Frees disk space occupied by stopped Django containers and their filesystem layers.
  • Environment Hygiene: Maintains clean Django development and production environments by removing unused containers.

Methods

Development Environment Cleanup

Syntax: docker compose rm -f

Parameters: --force (skip confirmation) for Django automated cleanup processes

Clean Django development environment by removing all stopped containers without data loss for fresh development cycles.

Production Maintenance

Syntax: docker compose rm --dry-run && docker compose rm -f web worker

Parameters: Preview and selective removal for Django production environment maintenance

Safe Django production cleanup with preview verification and selective container removal for specific services.

Return Value

Returns removal status for each Django service container showing successful deletion. Lists containers that were removed or skipped.

  • Success (0): All specified stopped containers removed successfully
  • Warning: No stopped containers found for specified services
  • Error (1): Container removal failure or permission issues

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Development Cycle Cleanup (Testing Environment Reset)

Scenario: Cleaning up stopped Django containers from multiple testing cycles while preserving Skills verification data, User profiles, and JobPost information for continued development.

# Preview containers to be removed
docker compose rm --dry-run

# Remove stopped containers safely
docker compose rm -f

# Verify volume preservation and start fresh
docker volume ls | grep anihpj && docker compose up -d

docker compose config

Official Docs: docker compose config | Docker CLI: docker compose config

Parse and validate Django Compose file configuration displaying resolved service definitions.

Full Description

The docker compose config command parses your anihpj Django compose file and outputs the resolved configuration, showing how services, networks, volumes, and environment variables are interpreted. This validates syntax, resolves variable substitutions, and displays the final configuration that Docker Compose will use.

For Django applications, this command is essential for debugging configuration issues, validating environment-specific settings, confirming service dependencies, and understanding how compose files merge together. It helps ensure your anihpj jobpost application configuration is correct before deployment.

Syntax

# Show complete resolved configuration
docker compose config

# Show only service names
docker compose config --services

# Show configuration for specific service
docker compose config web

# Show in JSON format
docker compose config --format json

# Validate without output
docker compose config --quiet

# Show volumes configuration
docker compose config --volumes

# Show configuration with secrets
docker compose config --no-interpolate

# Show profiles information
docker compose config --profiles

Parameters Description

  • --services: List only Django service names defined in compose file. Quick overview of available services.
  • --volumes: List only volume names for Django data persistence. Verify volume configurations and names.
  • --format json: Output Django configuration in JSON format. Machine-readable format for automated processing.
  • --quiet: Validate Django compose file without output. Silent syntax and configuration validation.
  • --no-interpolate: Show raw Django configuration without variable substitution. Debug environment variable issues.
  • Service Name: Show configuration for specific Django service. Focus on individual service settings.

Attributes

  • Configuration Validation: Validates Django compose file syntax and structure, ensuring proper YAML format.
  • Variable Resolution: Resolves environment variables and substitutions in Django configuration for final values.
  • Service Dependencies: Shows resolved Django service dependencies and network connections between components.
  • Environment Merging: Displays merged configuration from multiple Django compose files and overrides.
  • Output Formatting: Supports multiple output formats for Django configuration analysis and automation.

Methods

Configuration Validation

Syntax: docker compose config --quiet

Parameters: --quiet for Django compose file syntax validation without output

Validate Django compose file syntax and configuration correctness before deployment or testing.

Service Configuration Analysis

Syntax: docker compose config web

Parameters: service name for focused Django service configuration review

Examine specific Django service configuration including ports, volumes, environment variables, and dependencies.

Return Value

Returns resolved Django configuration in YAML or JSON format showing final service definitions and settings.

  • Success (0): Valid configuration displayed or validated successfully
  • Validation Error (1): Invalid syntax or configuration errors found
  • File Error (2): Compose file not found or not readable

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Production Configuration Validation (Environment-Specific Settings)

Scenario: Validating production Django configuration for anihpj deployment including User authentication settings, JobPost processing queues, Skills verification services, and Location-based search with proper environment variable resolution.

# Validate complete production configuration
docker compose -f docker-compose.yml -f docker-compose.prod.yml config --quiet

# Show resolved production configuration
docker compose -f docker-compose.yml -f docker-compose.prod.yml config

# Verify environment-specific settings
docker compose config --format json | jq '.services.web.environment'

        if check == 'django_models_accessible' or check == 'models_schema_ready':
            check_name = check.replace('_', ' ').title()
            models = ', '.join(result) if isinstance(result, list) else str(result)
            print(f"      ✅ {check_name}: {models}")
        else:
            check_name = check.replace('_', ' ').title()
            status_icon = "✅" if result is True or result == "enabled" else "❌" if result is False else "ℹ️"
            print(f"      {status_icon} {check_name}: {result}")

docker compose top

Official Docs: docker compose top | Docker CLI: docker compose top

Display running processes in Django service containers showing system resource usage and activity.

Full Description

The docker compose top command displays the running processes within your anihpj Django service containers, showing process IDs, CPU usage, memory consumption, and command details. This provides real-time insight into what's happening inside each container and helps monitor resource utilization.

For Django applications, this command is essential for performance monitoring, debugging application behavior, identifying resource bottlenecks, and understanding process activity in your anihpj jobpost application. It helps track Django workers, database connections, cache processes, and background tasks.

Syntax

# Show processes for all services
docker compose top

# Show processes for specific service
docker compose top web

# Show processes with extended information
docker compose top -e

# Monitor specific Django services
docker compose top web db redis

# Show processes in specific format
docker compose top --format table

# Continuous monitoring (with watch)
watch -n 2 "docker compose top"

# Show worker processes only
docker compose top worker

Parameters Description

  • Service Names: Specify which Django services to monitor. Focus on specific containers like web, worker, or db.
  • -e, --extended: Show extended process information for Django containers including environment and arguments.
  • --format: Output format for Django process display. Control how process information is presented.
  • Multiple Services: Monitor several Django services simultaneously. View processes across web, database, and cache services.
  • Watch Integration: Combine with watch command for continuous Django process monitoring and real-time updates.

Attributes

  • Process Monitoring: Real-time view of Django application processes including web servers, workers, and background tasks.
  • Resource Tracking: Shows CPU and memory usage for Django processes, helping identify performance bottlenecks.
  • Service-Specific View: Filter Django process display by service type for focused monitoring of specific components.
  • System Integration: Leverages host system process table to show Django container process activity and resource consumption.
  • Debugging Support: Identifies running Django processes for troubleshooting, performance analysis, and optimization.

Methods

Performance Monitoring

Syntax: docker compose top web

Parameters: service name for focused Django web server process monitoring

Monitor Django web server processes including Gunicorn workers, request handlers, and resource utilization patterns.

Background Task Monitoring

Syntax: docker compose top worker

Parameters: worker service for Django Celery task and background job monitoring

Track Django background task execution including job processing, queue management, and worker activity.

Return Value

Returns formatted table of Django service processes showing PID, CPU%, MEM%, command, and process status information.

  • Success (0): Process information displayed successfully
  • No Processes (0): Services running but no processes to display
  • Service Error (1): Specified service not found or not running

5 Practical Django Examples

Example 1: Production Performance Monitoring (High-Load Process Analysis)

Scenario: Monitoring production Django processes during peak traffic handling User authentication, JobPost search operations, Skills verification requests, and Location-based filtering with real-time performance analysis.

# Monitor all Django services during peak load
docker compose top

# Focus on web server processes
docker compose top web

# Monitor background workers
docker compose top worker

# Extended process information
docker compose top -e web worker

print(f"\n🐳 Service Process Analysis:")
for service, details in service_process_monitoring.items():
    service_name = service.replace('_service', '').replace('_', ' ').title()
    container = details['container_name']
    process_count = details['process_count']
    
    print(f"\n   📋 {service_name} Service ({container}):")
    print(f"      Process Count: {process_count}")
    
    if 'performance_metrics' in details:
        metrics = details['performance_metrics']
        print(f"      Total CPU: {metrics['total_cpu_usage']:.1f}%")
        print(f"      Total Memory: {metrics['total_memory_mb']}MB")
        print(f"      Avg Response: {metrics['average_response_time']}")
    
    print(f"      Key Processes:")
    for process in details['processes'][:3]:  # Show first 3 processes
        purpose = process['purpose'].replace('_', ' ').title()
        print(f"        - PID {process['pid']}: {purpose}")
        print(f"          CPU: {process['cpu_percent']:.1f}% | Memory: {process['memory_mb']}MB")
        if 'models_served' in process:
            models = ', '.join(process['models_served'])
            print(f"          Django Models: {models}")

    if 'model_operations' in details:
        print(f"      Model Operations:")
        for model, ops in details['model_operations'].items():
            total_ops = sum(ops.values())
            print(f"        📊 {model}: {total_ops} operations")

print(f"\n💾 Database Performance:")
db_metrics = service_process_monitoring['db_service']['database_metrics']
print(f"   Active Connections: {db_metrics['active_connections']}")
print(f"   Connection Pool Usage: {db_metrics['connection_pool_usage']}")
print(f"   Cache Hit Rate: {db_metrics['query_cache_hit_rate']}")
print(f"   Slow Queries: {db_metrics['slow_query_count']}")

for model, perf in db_perf.items():

    print(f"\n   📊 {model_name.title()} Table:")
    print(f"      Size: {perf['size']} | Queries/Min: {perf['queries_per_minute']}")
    print(f"      Index Usage: {perf['index_usage'].title()} | Hit Rate: {perf['cache_hit_rate']}")

print(f"\n🔄 Background Workers:")
worker_metrics = service_process_monitoring['worker_service']['task_metrics']
